An answer to the deuillish detection of Stephane Gardener, Bishop of
Wynchester, published to the intent that such as be desirous of the truth
should not be seduced by his errors, nor the blind and obstinate excused by
ignorance.

Compiled by. A. G.

Iudicum. vi. Oh let the^ perish from the earth, and from under the heaven, all
the Idols that have not made the heaven and the earth, destroy you their
groves and altares, If they be gods let them reueng them selves.

Anno. 1547. the. 24, of January

In the viii. leaf i. page and xiiii. line: for stain mne, read, same mine.

To the Reader.
Dearly beloved (bought with the same blood, and therefore part takers of the
same kyngedome) because the Lord our God is the God of knowledge, and will
have such servants as by knowledge in truth without fleshely fantasies,
either of fained gods or any fond worship of man's mad brain (who always
from the beginneinge has run after vanities) will be radie to give answer
of their faieth in him, the God of life and of the hope conceived by his only
word: it becomes all his ^o labor for knowledge, that they may walk
upright in the way of their Lord, and by no halting ignorance to slide forth
of the same and so to provoke his worthi displeasure. And as he is the God of
love, peace, unity and concord, and will have us al tied together with the
bond of love and made thereby (in him) all one body: so does it become us
with open hertes, without all doubleness, one to enstructe an other, to the
edifiynge of our brethern, that in sure grownded faith we may love together
and so enjoy the hope of our vocacion. Therefore, though mi talent be very
small and no principal gift either of eloquence or learning, but only a love
of the truth given unto me, yet saying the world is so blinded with
Idolatry, and so beewitched with popish sophistry, and even now the
spirittes and powers of darcknes work the chief mystery of iniquity and
wickedness, to set up and maintain the most weak Idol that ever was in the
world, in the stead of the most mighty and euerliuinge God: I could think
it no less the^ my most bounden duty, openly to bear witness unto the
truth. And where as the words of truth, have been slandrously and spitfully
named the saieinges of the devil by the spiritual craft of a soldier of
Satan, which by painted words would transform him self into an angel of
light. Whose book is spread every where, and received in many places more
reverently then the blessed bible, the holy word of God. Yet no man has (so
far as I know) once opened his mouth or taken pen in hand, to make answer
to this blasphemouse messenger of the proud Senacherib neglectinge the
liueinge God, for the littel I dole that he makes God or no God at his
pleasure, who suffers Mise to eat him and the wicked to devour him. Let
all other men do as they shall thyncke good, with silence to let such things
slip. Truly if I could say nothing thereunto but only nay, denienge
Idolatry and renouncing all supersticion therein maintained: I judge it my
part to publishe my faith, rather then by my silence to seame to consent to
such diuillishe doctrine. So also do I esteem it the duty of the faithful in
this perilous time, plainly to profess the Lord the liueuinge God, to be the
only God in heaven a boue and in the earth beneth: lest by our silence for
sakinge his cause here upon earth, we be forsaken in his heavenly palace. For
like as in heart we do believe to our righteousness: so must we necessarily
confess to our salvation, as Paul teachethe. ii. Corh. xi.


We must beware (as Paul warnethe, and the bishope takes the same text) first
ofal, that our senses be not corrupted from the simplicite and sing lenesse
that is in Christ, as the serpent begiled Eua. We know but one God. We are
married unto one. We know but one Christ made man and none other creature for
ourcause. This thing as we believe it in heart: so must we in mouth ^o^fesse
the same, if we will walk in the simplicity and sing linesse that is in
Christ, as becomes christians. For if the heart and mouth go together, then is
it sing lenesse, otherwise it is doubleness and dissembling. But there is one
other simplicity (as it has been compted, and as the word has been abused)
which is very folishnes. This may we call the simplicity, that Antichriste
would have still to reign among us, and therefore his champion, when he
brought in the text of Paulle: left out the principal words (Que est in
christo) Which is in Christ, as their old text has it. And through out his
whole book, he would drive us to be simple. That is to say, to follow as we
be led like blind men: that the proud papisticall prelates, still leadeinge
us into the pit of perdicion, abuseing our wines and goods, may say in
their connentes. Let them alone, let them offer still unto Imeages, a pice of
bread or any thing else of a good intent, all is well done that is done of a
good intent,

They may worship a stock or a stone, let them follow their ancient fathers.
They are good simple souls. They do as we and our doctors teach the^. If we
let the^ know al truth: they will be as wise as we, and then they will smally
regard us. This is their workeinge, these are their words, how so ever they
have clok^d hertofore, all the word now sees it. Let us beware therefore, of
this their simplicity, and let us no longer think that this their doctrine
is'true, that al should he well done that is done for a good intent, and that
it is well done in all things to believe their doctors. For this ignorante
opinion that they have grounded in their hertes has hitherto stopped the way
to all knowledge, and now lets faith to be grounded and causes men to
continue still in their old errowres, without any desire to come out of
blindness. Consider therefore (good reader) a gaynste their blind lessons:
that Saull was cast from his kyngedome, for his good intent, even because he
intended to do sacrifice unto the Lord, of the best and fatteste of the
Amalechites. And yet may this seem a gloriouse intent.

The bishops of the Jews and the Idolatours of al ages followed their good
intent: even when they put Christ and all his prophets and Apostles to death.
The bishop of Norwich when he burned pore Bilney, followed his good intent our
other byshopes also, burneninge and murtheringe their brethren in prisone and
out of prisone: followed their good in tents, But God is the judge of the
inte^tes and thoughts of us al, and sercheth the very rain and the holes of
our hertes. Yea the lord our god abhors and the prophets reprove us
always: because we will do every man that seems good in his own eyes

Says not the Lord by his prophet Esaye. Mine intentes are not your in
ente^s, and mi ways are not your ways. But ^o, so far as the heaven is from
the earth, so high are my ways above your ways, and mine intentes above your
intentes. For the belief of their doctors and the prelates of the church
(which thing the bishop labors always to establish) remember that
Christ says, if the blind lead the blind: boeth fall into the pit. And
thou must doub tlesse co^mpt their writtinges eue^ very blindness, in regarde^
of the light of gods most certain word which must be the rule of thy life,
the fou^dacion of thy faith, and the light unto thy feet. As for their
auncientie: be sure to take Christ for they guide, who was before all. And say
with S. Paul, faith is of heariuge, not of the word of any man: but of the
word of God.

Therefore says God the father with open voice from heaven. This is my
dearly beloved son in whom is my delight, hear you him.

Now if any be so fainte herted and so deluded by other, that they thyncke they
may still disseinble with the hypocrites in their owtwarde doetnges: I send
them to the exemple of Daniel, who prayed with open windows, and (with his
three companions) refused to honor the golden Image, and would not dissemble
outward worship, another content them selves with the pureness of their own
hertes (though they might thereby have escaped the fire) consideringe that the
glory of God could not be so fo^dered, but rather hindered by their walkeinge
in the way of the wicked. Therefore says the prophet David. Happy is he that
nether stands sits nor walks (that is to say) has nothing Psal^.
to do with them, other openly or privily, by any color or dissimulacion.

Eliazar had such like counsel of his friends, that he should eat flesh
only which ii. Match. vii.
was lawful, and dissemble to eat the unlawful. But he said it was not
lawful for him to dissemble, and so cause many to be deceived through his
hypocrisy: for so he might escape the death of the body, but the hand of God
he could not avoid. For this cause did Paul reprove Peter for his
dissemblinge be fore the gentiles. And he teaches the Corinthians Galat. ii.
again, that there is no company of light and darckenesse, no dessemblinge to
be partaker boeth of the cup of Christ and of deuilles.

Our members must be the weapons either of rightuousenes, other else of
vnrighttuousenesse, there is no mean for still and ware politic persons. And
therefore says our master Christ, he that is not with me is against me. And
he that does not gather, does scatter. These words of Christ and such
like, and none other cause (whatsoever any man shall imagine) have compelled me
to publish my faith, and in the name of the liueinge God, to make answer to
one book, which of all other I esteemed most perilouse and poysonful, boeth for
the authorite of the writter, and the subtle handellinge of his mattier in the
maytaineinge of that Idol, which all the world has worshipped so many years.
The name of the book is the detection of the diuillysh sophistry. The author
that made it is Stephaue Gardener, bishop of Winchester, the chief mantainer
of the popeishe tradicions, as appears by all his deeds and writings. How I
have used my self in the same: I shall show at few words.

Because I did take upon hand to confute his book: I could keep no comely
order but as the words do lead me, so am I compelled to go forward. Yet have
I not written his whole text in my book (because it would* have been to much
tediouse and over long but only his* chief, mattier and principal
arguments, whereof I trust not one has escaped untouched. I lest of the
residue, thinkeing it a very vain thing to contend about trifles, as I
should have done of necessi^e, in waigheinge every word and ponderinge every
sentence. The book is so far spread a broabe, that I can not belie him but it
shall be a witness against me, in every corner. For it was plentuousely
imprinted by John Herforde in aldergate street at London, and is to be sold at
the sign of the bell in poules church yard. I have principally and chief
labored to establishe the true fayeth in the liueinge God: by the reproueinge
of the false and fained goods. Secondly, I have taught the trwe understanding
of the words of the supper of the Lord, and the right use of the same. Which
two my chief purposes how faithfully I have done them: the fathfull shall
judge, knowing the voice of of their shepeherde.

In mine answer to his words, I trust no man shall be offended with any
vnchrist an rayleinges, though great accasio^ be offerred on his part,
bringeinge our arguments so spitfully in the name of devil, with yea, says
the deuell, as though the deuell where a destroier of Idols, wh^e only has
been their mainetainer and vpholder, from the be geninge of the world unto
this day. Yet I do think nothing less, then to satisfy all men with my
writtinges, more then other have done before mi time, with theirs, much more
witty, more learned and godly. No, I do suppose, the hight learned may find
many fautes there'with, as I* acknowledge mi self far under the perfection of
their high lerninge. Nevertheless, I trust in God that it is not all together
so rude nor unfruitful: but that the unlearned (for whom it is chief lie
written) shall increase by it in knowledge, cast of much supersticion, and
take conforte of conscience. Whom also I beseech, even for the love* of God,
and* as they tender their souls health: not to cast away this bokethough
they read something therein that they never hard before, but rather desire of
their most merciful father, that their old errors wherewith they have been
deceived by blind teachers, may be taken away. And if there be any that can
not sodaineli cast of the old skine with the serpent and forsak their old
ignorance confirmed with long custom: let the^ desir of God so much grace
that they may more quietly then has been accustomed, hear men talk of the
faith they have conceived in the liueinge God. For than shall it be well with the
christian religion: when the one part may boldly, and will redily give
answer of the hope they have conceived, and faith whereby they trust to be
saved, and the other part will mekeli hear what is spoken, and quietely
suffer the lambs to feed of their sweet pasturs. So shall the prophecy be
fulfilled. The lamb shall lodge with the woulfe, the leoparde and Esaye. xi.
the go^e shall lie together. The calfe, the lion and the sheep shall dwell
together, and a little child shall be their herd and drive them, which thing I
trust partly shall be fullfilled in our time under our little Josias, to whom
God grant the abundaunce of his grace. And most fully under the true Josias
Christ Jesus our savior, who only is the end of all prophecies, in whom
they al are made perfect, with whom we shall enjoy this perfect peace, so
many as defire to know the living God, and whom he sent down to save the
world Jesus Christ, now sitting at his right hand, to whom be glory For
ever and ever. So be it

John. iiii. Episto. i. Who so knows God hears us. An^ he that is not of
God hears not us. And herby do we know, the spirit of truth, and the
spirit of errowre.
The Prologue.
GRace and peace from the Lord the liueinge God, who has all our hertes in
his hand to move and stere to what shall like him best, who only knows the
hertes of men, and therefore oneli is the judge of the thoughts and intentes
of us all, what or when so ever we speak or think. whose day and judgment is
without regard what man (which is but flesh and blood, and therefore full of
error and blindness) shall dispute, and determine and judge. I patiently
look for and a bide when as all darnell, drake and weed shall be cast into
the hell fire and all the good grain shall be gathered into God his own
garner, unto whom we live all the time that we walk upon the earth. And when
we die yet are we sure that we are his own, by the ransom that his dearly
beloved sone Christ (our Lord and head) has paid geueinge the holy ghost into
our hertes as a most suer witness of the same, teacheinge us to cry. Aba
father, whereby we know that though we die, yet we die unto him to live ever
after cowpled and joined in one kind and nature unto our head Christ, who as
he is fully God, and of equale power with his father, so shall he make us like
unto him when he shall appear (after our portion and measure) partakers of his
godly nature, like as he has in his world (though but in a shadow and cloud,
in regard of the fullness that shall be declared) be gonne al ready to regenerate
and begete us a new* creature, by the holy ghost workinge by the word of his
truth, that we now resembling the image of God whereunto we were made, may
be continually occupied in the works of his kingdom, as be these. Justice,
peace* and joy in the same holy ghost, geuear of al goodness. For he that by
these works serves Christ is acceptable to God and conmended of men This
some ^^e ever lasteinge God without begininge and without endinge, he give me
grace (to the fortheraunce of his glory) to make answer to that deuellishe
detection the sophistry of Satan published by Stephane Gardener bishope of
Winchester, for the maintenance of the popish Idol, the dombe God, and
poetical chaungling, where by, not only the true living God is neglected his
true honor obscured and defaced, the preachinge of his word almost set at
naught: but also, all kinds of popery, as images, blessing, kissinge,
shaueinge of crowns, supersticio^ of garmenets and such like, are craftily, by
subtle points of the popes sophistri and words filthy, framed for such
merchaundise, confirmed and established, as thought all the whole heap of these
triffes heaped up together were the religion of a Christian man: where as to
know God for our true God, and whom hehath sent, Jesus Christ, and by this
knowledge to be borne a new and to keep our self immaculate and vnde filed
from the world is: the true and perfect religion demanded of us true
christians. The other is but countrefaite what so ever ^his sophistry does
name it) because our master christ (who can not lie) does say full plain.
(...).

They worshipe me in vain, teacheinge the doctrine and precepts of men etc.
And where he brings in this text in the end of his book, nothing so full as
our savior Christ did speak it (as he knows well inowgh if he have so much
Greek as he braggeth abroad) he adds thereunto his own gloss, as though he
could utter the words of christ the sone of God, much more wisely by his
babbling. Yet am I content to let his own gloss be his own judge in these
matters. His words be these. They worship me in vain, with the teachinge
of such as remain in the estate of men only, and the^ teach their own and
for the^ selves, for all such teachinge is like the teachar that is to say
carnal. Let eueri man (that has not his conscience al ready brenned with the
hot pro^e) mark whether his own gloss make against him, and all the
ceremonies that his father the pope, being (I trow) but in the estate of a
man, and that a carnal man, has made, though Winchester go about craftily
(according to the cannon law whereof he is sworn by solemn oath doctoure
and teacher) to make him more the^ a man. And mark again good christen
hertes, what they win by their gloses and multiplied words, whereby in faith it
were very easy to confute them all, even by the testimonies of their own
doctors (as Bucere, Ecolampadius, and Frith have done perfectly well, if
these men would suffer there books to come to light) For these papists do so
mixte the truth and salsehed together (for without some ground of truth noman
would believe them) that the one piece of the tale stands commonly with the
truth and the other utters their salshed.

And therefore speak they long matter and are not content to say plainly a
spade but they must necker it as they do in their mattens and say, spa^a
a^ade. As for me I have learned to call bread, bread, and to speak althinges
plainly. Therefore by the open scriptures, will I make them answer to their
questions. For all the scripture inspired from God, is profitable boeth to
teach and to reprove, to correct and to instruct in righteousness, that the
man of God may be perfect and fite for every good work.

So that if there be any* good work* to be taught or ill worck ^o be rebuked we
must go to the scripture only, as to the toutchstone and only trial of al
truth.

For with scriptures did Christ drive away the devil, and not with holy
water, as you are reported to say that the devil greatly dreadeth it, and so
do ye still command that it shall be made a coniured water every sonnedayes
in* every church, to drive forth deuilles. But he though he were boeth god
and man, alleges scriptures always to confirm his saienges, and commands
his hearers to sherch the scriptures. So do Peter, Paul, James, and John.

Whereas Paul being brought up at the fete of Gamaliell the great lawier, was
ready inoughe to have disputed out of the Thalmud of the tradicions of their
fathers, which he says he has ernestely studied being ou^ of the
phariseies, and interpretour of that law, and such one as by the outward words
of the law could not be found fantie, Gala. i. Phili. iii.
Yet did he acco^pte all this, boeth lerneinge and outward holiness (which
other men did take as no small gainne and ^^cre) to be damage and hindrance for
Chirst, whom so sone as he was called to publishe and preach he did not compare
with the docters of the Jews, neither with Gamaliell, Annas or Laiphas. But
knoweinge his learneinge to be more lively than was theirs (which being but
f^esh and blood, could teach only carnal and f^eshly things) went straight
in to Arabie, there to publishe this glade tidinges, ever teachinge by the
scriptures that Christ, did come this to suffer in the flesh, and that he was
after that, entered into his glory.

So do I intend (after the measure of my talent) to answer by the lernige of
my master Christ, whom only. I do take to be al sufficiens in all truth, so
that he can neither be deceived nor deceive, to whose wisdom no man can add
one jot or title to make better that he has made, to institute or ordeine
(whose whether you will call it, because ye are so contenciouse, about trifles
that you may seem to say some what) better then he him self has* instit^ted
and ordained, or yet in speak better then'he has spoken. And in this be
half, I must (even of brotherly love) desire all indifferent arbitours and
judges of my writings, that if they do read any bitter word or hear any
sharp sentence against the mainteiners of this Idol: they do not impu^e it
to any pride or arrogancy but to the unworthiness of the matter, that man
should be so mad to set up a creature most vile and most weak in the stead
of the Lord of hosts whose pouer is incomparable. In the which thing, being a
cause (...) so great importance, and weight if I should coldely or faintly
speak or write I might well be thought worthy to be one of them whom John
prophecieth, for their faynte hertes, worthy to be v^etted up again, being
nether hot nor cold. I do fear me the plage of God has worthyly commen upon
many in this same royalme, for this only vice. But God, he is merciful if we
will repent.

As for me O Lord thou knoweste al things, thou knoweste mine heart, and
serchestmy thoughts. Thou woteest that it is neither of malice nor presumption
that I do write any word in this book, but only for the pride of the papists,
and especially for the wicked malice of proud A man, which seaketh how to
destroy thy servants, labourethe to oppress thy light sent now in these
la^er days at the time appointed, into the world, provoke us with bitter
words, to make answer in thy cause, calling us diueles, and the reasones made
against Idolatry for the an anseinge of thy glory, he calls the dy^eles
words and saieinges, which blasphemies cause me that I can not give place but
something answer to his worthiness, and not give place to such shameless
writings.

Though I could be content (and that with good will so that it were no
derogacion to thy glory) not only to pass with silence all tau^tes, rebukes,
che^kes, and raileinges, yea and to suffer all cruelty and tirannus torments
that he does excogitat or find out against us: but also to kiss his very
footsteps, and call him Lord at every word, to kneel and lowte as do his
flatterers. But then l^^e we forsake thy cause, we can not have thy word in
worthy reverence, magnifieinge thine enemy.

Take thou in good worth therefore (O Lord (these our doings. Make the^
serve thy glory. Be merciful to thy servants, and stop the mouth of thine
enemies that thy will may, be known and fulfilled among us in erath, as it is
among thin angels in thine heavenly palace So be it.

To your first words therefore (bishope Stephane, pardone me I pray you that
I do not call you Lord, boeth because I have learned by scripture that Christ's
byshopes Math. xxiii.
may take no such vain titles, and also that you ought to calenge no such
authorite of James. iii.
Lordeshipe over your lotte and people appointed unto you, and Peter and Paul,
the i. Peter. v.
good shepeherdes do we name without such vain titles of Rabby) you will have
us consider i. Chap. How full of iniquity that time is.
how full of iniquity this time is. Let us consider it for the love of God (O
bishopes) but not takeinge iniquity as you do, to be what so ever thing is
against the tradicions of your Romish father, who now works the chief
mystery of iniquity, and every one of you helps after to his pour, in
kepeinge down the word of God, clokeinge your hypocrisy with contrefaite
holiness, and tourneinge backewarde so far from Christ: that every man
may see who is the wicked man, and the adversary or Antichriste, lifteinge
him self against every thing that is God or godly, So that now your
shameless writings of your doctors and maintainers: do record how you can
make God, create the creatoure of heaven and er^h, and so make him a creature,
that where he has but once created the, thou maiste be out of his det and cre^
him a thousand times. Oh abominable blsasphemie A man to make God, at whose
terrible majesty, heaven and earth do tremble. Oh shamlesse iniquity, to
create thy creatoure without whom thou falleste in to duste and ashes. But
you will say (O bishope) that there is no such blasphemy in your books,
neither can you perceive the wickedness of the popes pardones, and pilgrimages
which are destroyed in this time, The Sodomatrie babilonical bondage,
supersticiouse blindness of the Abbaies, which our king has most
christenlyke confounded. But for this our mattier, I say. I plucked half a
leaf out of a book lieinge tied in chains for a Jewel in the great
cathedral church, Lincoln minstre, which has this plain greare, by these
plain words. O sacerdos, nonne creaui te, et dedi tibi potestatem creaudi me?
quare si non sacrificas, et c. O priest, have I not created the, and given the
pour ^o create me? And such other shamful gear.

There is none so blind as they that will not se. And saying such blindesse is
in you bishopes, who should have hade the eyes to have espied this ware long
before it hade ben brought into the churches contrary to the word of God: how
can it be but by your careless negligence, the world is waxen full of
blindness, misery and all kinds of iniquity, for the which you shall
answer at the dreadful day when the blood of every one of your sheep that
perishes shallbe required at your hand. Let us consider yet if you please,
this wickedness some thing more deaplye.

Paul in his first Epistle to the bishop Timo. i.
Timothe, says that the spirit tells for certain, that in the latter
days, some shall depart that diuil^ sophistry
from the fayeth, attendynge unto deceptfull spirits and doctrine of diuelles,
speakeinge falsely by dissemblinge hypocrisy haueinge their consciences marked
with the hot yrone.

And that we should not doubt of this devilish sophistry and open iniquite:
he adds two special properties, that is, to prohibit or forbid marriage, and
command to abstain from meats which God has created to be received with
thanks geueing, as the good ceatures of God. Who follows the diuelles
doctrine most in these to points: is not hard to be judged of all the world

Yet must we futhermore consider the spirit^es you say which thing we* are
not loath Believe not e^ie spirit. John. iiii.
to do (for John teaches us so) mistrusteinge our own judgment. And John
says that every spirit that confesses Jesus Christ to be come in the
flesh, is of God. This do we all confess, whom you call at your pleasure
heretics, and say that we will doubt in all together. But we knoweinge
certenlie John. i. Timo. iii.
by the scriptures, that he was manifestely declared in the flesh to be very
man, and perfectly declared in the spirit to be God in the wonderouse workinge
of his miracles, was seen among the angels, was believed in the world, and
received into glory, where he reigns equale with his father, sittinge at the
right hand of God, from whense we no thing doubt, but we shall se him come down
as the apostles did se him go up into the heauenes. Act. i. In the mean season
we believe steadfastly that he is with his faiethfull church by his holy spirit
even to the worlds Ephe. v.
end. For the which he gave him self to sanctify it and cleuse it, in the
fountain of water by the word, to make it unto him self a gloriouse
congregation without spot or wrynckle or any such thing, but that it should
be holy and without blame, Where contrary wise, you (which account your
selves only, men of the church) and spirirituall men, as the only partakers
of the spirit (do with out scripture or reasone) teach us lay and lewd men
(as ye call us) only with sword and fire, that Christ was not very man
haueinge a natural body. For you say that this his body that he had may be
in. x. thowsande places at once. Which property, how well it agreth with a
natural body: all that have any knowledge may decerne. Again you say that
this body of the same lengeth and breadeth that it hanged upon the cross:
may be closed in a little box, contrary to the ordinance of man's natural
body in the creacion. And where we se nothing but a piece of bread (for you
can not teach us by the scriptures that the bread is changed) we must neades
believe, that their is a body, besides the bread because you say so thought
there can be perceived neither quantity nor quality, that is to say,
nothing parteininge to a body. As for your answer of fayeth constrained to
believe this without either scripture or* reasone, that it may have merit, and
that all these be natural reasons: I shall answer when I come at those words.

In the mean time mark your own maliciouse wickedness, how you will have*

But first I will bring forth the whole text of Mathewe, Mark and Luke. And

Christ in the xxvi. of Mathewe, when he was together with his Apostles,
eateinge the passover (which was the most live like figure in the old law,
now making an end in Christ the lamb without all spo^e and blemishe) did
ordeine this godly sacrament, for the remembrance of him self to the world
folowinge: and that his death might be showed and published unto the worlds
and, like as in the passover was continually mentioned and declared, to the
posterity foloweinge, the benifite of God in the deliverance from Egypt. And
as that ceremony (the eateinge of the lamb) was called the passover, and he
him self called the lamb of god so like wise calls he this hight mystery
and sacrament, his body, and a new testament in his blood. That as truly as
the Israelites were delivered forth of Egipte the angel passing by not hurting
the people of that house (the door posts whereof were sprinkled with the blood
of that lamb) so verily should Christ deliver us out of the Egypt of sin,
and perform the thing before figured. For this cause says John, behold
the lamb of God, which takes away the sins of the world. And Luke xxii.
Christ says. This is my body which is given for you. And this cup is the
new testament in my blood, which is shede for you. By the which words it
may appear that Christ did mean no change of natures, or
traunssubstancion, but only that where the blood of the lamb in the old
testament was sprenkled on the posts to save from the aduengeinge angel so
many as should be saved: so likewise this blood of Christ in the new
testament should be shede to save us, so mani as have our souls sprink led
with the blood of this lamb Christ Ies^. Therefore, in like manner as the
fathers of the old law drank of the spiritual ston that followed them*
(which was Christ) even so are we all commanded to drink of this blood,
none other wise then the children of Israel were commanded, that the blood
of the lamb should be their token in all the houses where they were. There was

The resolusion of certain doubts contained in Winchesters book
THus have I put you out of doubt* that we doubt in no article of the
christian faith. But I doubt that you b^e not yet out of doubt in those
things that you doubt of in your detection, amongst which this is the
greatest doubt. You doubt (you say) how the son of god whom you call Jesus)
should be contained in the womb of the virgin. Unto this your boubt, I
answer, that as he was and is God: so was* he and is without beginning and
end. And the heaven, yea the heaven of Apocal. xxii. iii Reg. viiii.
al heavens, can not contain him (much less a littlle box to be shut therein
(but as he was very man, so was it true that the prophet did speak. That a
woman should compass a man. And this body (that was borne of of the woman)
can you not prove to be scatterred throught out all corners of the earth and to
be in heaven also. For so should you make him a spirit and no body (yea all
together God and no crature, for no creature can be in ^o places the^ one at
one) co^trari to the chieffest article of our faith, which is that he was
incarnat and became man like unto us in all things (sin only excepted) and
that in the same flesh he dyed once, rose again, and ascended into heaven,
and there sits at the right hand of God the father, from when (...) he
shall come even very man as he asended, Acto. i.
having all the propreties of an incorruptible body, that is to say, being
visible and local, haueing quantity and qualities as his fayethfull disciples
and Apostles saw and perceined him to have after his resurrection which
proprites declared him to di^^er from a spirit (much more from God) as
concerneinge the body wherein these qualitites be. The godheade differs and
is known from the body by that it is immense, and can be contained in no
place neither is it sensible, nor can be perceived by any of the senses. Where
as contrariwyse, the body is sensible and may be boeth felt and seen, and
must needs be always contained in some one place, other else is it no body.
And thought by miracle, God have carried any corporal body from place to
place, contrary to the course of nature as he did Elias, in the firely chariot.
Or as iiii. Reg. ii.
he carried Abacuke for the confort of daniell, and as the spirit of God took
away Philip, when he had christened the Ennuche of queen Candaces, and set him
at Azotu^. And Acto. viii
as by the spirit, Peter was brought out of prisone, taken from the four
quaternians of soldiers, his body lowsed forth of all the chains and
prisons sodaynelye, yea the Act. xii.
^ate of Irone openeinge against him, contrary to the natural order: yet can
no man prove by these or any like miracle, that one body has been in. ii.
places at once, much les that any of these bodies may be eueri where, as you
do maynetayne (by miracle of Christ comeinge into the house when the Apostles
had shette the doors and wyndowes, for the fear of the Jews) that the natural
body of Christ may be in ten thousand boxes and aultres, when you do not
know whether the doors did open against Christ as the Iron gate did against
Peter. But you bring in your sophistry against al reasone, with out any
scripture, and therefore without any fayeth, affirmeinge that. ii. bodies are in
one place together and occupi the same place at one time, which neither faieth,
reasone, nor any of the se^ses (that ought by the ordinau^^ of God to judge of
all bodily things) could at any time, either by miracle or otherwise
perceive. Act. v.


We read in the. v. of the Acts, that the sect of the Sadduceis, did cast
the Apostles into prisone, and that they were brought fourth by an angel. Yet
when the ministers were sent to bring them to examinacion, they found the
prison diligently shot and the kepers standeinge at the gates. But now it
were a very slender reason, to prove that the bodies of the Apostles may be
in many pla^^es at once. And yet is this even like matter with the entering in
of Christ to his Apostles when the doors were shette. But boeth these miracles
were wrought to confirm the faith of the Apostles, not that Christ might lie
hid in a little bread, for they never taught this fayeth to the world. But
this was their doctrine, that their God could deliver from prisone, and raise
from death, for as much as he was the trwe God, even Christ Jesus the soune of
the lyueinge God, whom they preachede to be as then risen from death.

But you are not contented with this because it has some shadow of the of the
truth your purpose is to deceive by snbtyle words, But now you myxt open
falsehod and say that Christ did rise out of the grave the same being still
shet, where all the four evangelists do witness against you sayeing that the
stone was taken away or roled from the door of the grave or monument. It is no
marvel therefore, thought you would banishe as many as is possible from
readeinge of the scripture, for if no man might read the scripture but you and
your co^pleis then might you lie at the large without ^heke, and play your
legerdemayne without being esspied of any man. First John, the John, xx.

the stone tak^ away from the grave. And Matthew tells* how the stone was
taken away* The Angel of the Lord (says he) did come dow^ Mat. xxviii.
from heaven and did roll the stone from the door and sit upon it.

In Mark and Luke (good christians) yo^ may read (if the bishop will give

better seen in the popes lerning the^ inthe gospel of Christ. Who so lists to
be deceived: let them trust such byshopes

More over, lest it should seem strange to you that the graves should open:

and many bodies of the saints which were dead did rise, and after the

this by faith, that god is inviolable impassible, incorruptible, immortal,

All this is plain against your own The answer.
doctrine, for saying that the body of bread is clean gone, and yet there
remains a body that the mouse or ape catches in his mouth (or e^s they
could not carry it awey) What shall we conclude by your doctrine: but that the
mouse or ape runs away with that body which by your enchauntment, is
conceived into the place of the bread, which (blasphemously) do name the body
of Christ consecrated into the form of bread? But, you do answer, that like
as Christ when he was here in the flesh, did first escape the hands of
Herod, when he slew the children, and afterward the furious Jews, when they
would have precipitate him: transiens per Math. iij. Luke. iiii.
medium illorum ibat. Christ escapped through the midst of them. So does he
now say you. Your similitude is evil applied. For besides that there is no
comparison of Christ coming in the flesh for the wealth of the world, unto
the bread thus altered for your pomp and pride: we know, and Joseph and Mary
do witness unto us that they knew and perceived by the benifite of their
senses, that this same our Savior Christ was in shape a very man. And we
know also (by the testimonies of the scriptures) that he continued here very
man in form and shape, being subjected unto all our infirmities (sin
always excepted) for the space of. xxx. years and more, and that then he
suffered death and rose again, his flesh neither being consumed nor
putrified, but still remains flesh incorruptible and immortal. Where as in
the form of bread (wherein you say we see him and eat him) we perceive
neither incorruption nor immortality. For it never continues paste the date
of one month (if you incur not the danger of your fathers decrees) and
commonly not one quarter of an hour, much after the rate of the daily new
created monstros, of who^ Aristotle makes mention. Who doubtless if he had
hard of these monstrous gods (made and marred all in an hour) would have
written wonders unto his posterity. If the cakes were preserved from
corruption and did continewe still immortal, as Christ his flesh did: then
would your similitude (in these two miracles) serve you somewhat better. But
seeing that your cakes do mould and corrupt, and his flesh escaped Herod, and
the hands of his enemies, and could Psalm. xv.
never see any corruption: this your similitude proves, that those cakes of
yours can by no means be his natural body. These two miracles therefore (as
all his other) were done to declare him to be subject to no power of man, but
to work all his works so, that no man can let and hyndre ought that he has
determined to be done, but you must wrest all that you can, to cloak your
Sophistry wythall.

Now, your affirmation of. xv. hundred years without any proof, but only
because you say so: has been answered by many learned men. As ^adinius,

Understand, that the true church has always had this belife of Christ.

Upon this I demand, what you do The answer.
mean by this term Sacrament. If you say that a Sacrament is a sign or
remembrance of an holy thing (as all your own Doctors have defined a
Sacrament) then will we say (as the truth is, and as we have taught
heretofore) that this is the most holy sign, and blessed remembrance of
Christ our Savior, which offered his body for our sins, and commanded us
to frequent and use the same in the remembrance of him, who dyed once for us,
and sits now at the right hand of God, a perpetual mean between God and
man. And hear is the full profit, use and commodity that any man can have by
this Sacrament. Yet this will not satisfy you, unless you have us so
captive, that we will say after you. The Sacrament is the self same thing
that it signifies. Christ must be made in the remembrance of Christ. I
demand of you in all other things, be they holy or profane, where you ca^
find me one thing that is both the sign and the thing it self. The holy
Sacrament of Baptism is not so. The holy Sacrament of circumcision was not
so. The holy Sacrament of the Paschal lamb, was never named so in the old
testamente. Yet had they as plain words for them, as you have for yours. For
the circumcision is called the covenant, and the lamb is called the
passeo^er. But you will have the Sacrament to be the thing it self, and the
sign to be the Savior. For this intent no fail, that you being but the
signs and shadows Marcke my Lords intent
of true Bishops, your two forked cappes and labelles, the signs of much
holiness and knowledge in both the testame^tes, your white raichet, the sign of
chastity and pureness, your precio^s shoes, the signs of precious fnote
steps in preaching the Gospel: may be accounted the very things the^ selves
that be signified. So should we neither look into heaven for our only Savior
sitting at the right hand of his father, nor yet for true holiness in you upon
earth, being satisfied by your signs and shadows, your lyinge Poprie, dombe
and deceyueable ceremonies. It follows in your text.

When we call the Sacrament of the aultare God, we understand the substance of
Winchesters words
the Sacrament, which is Christ God and man there present. And according to
that understanding, we attribute al goodly honor unto it. And in this speech,
the word Sacrament, signifies and gives understanding by a special
significacion, and by excellency (as learned men speak of it) the thing
signified, being there present, that is to say, the body and blood of our
Savior Christ, which can not be broken with hand, ca^ not be torn with
teeth, or denoured of beasts, or putrified. Neither can the bodily senses,
herein bear any witness to the contrary, for they can not atteyne that. But
when we use the word, Sacrament, or the word, host, and apply the speech
of it to such a matter as may not be said of the natural body of Christ:
then the speech is verified in those forms of bread and wine, under the
which the most preciouse body and blood of Christ is covered, as when we say
the sacrament is broken or molded, or altered, it is only understood of the
said form of bread and wine, being the outward accide^tes as the qualities
or dime^tio^s, which god there preserves not otherwise by outward miracle,
being the^ sustained: by his most preciouse bodily substance. Then when they
be naturally joined to the substance of bread, whereof that God thus does not,
man's senses (because those accidents be sensile) may Judge for we se it so and
those accidents be perceptible, by the bodelie sight and sense* and with the
eye of the soul in faieth, we se the presence of our most blessed savior
Christ, who there is the only substance of the sacrament, so long remayninge
under those accidents, as the form of bread and wine, under which (by the
omnipote^cie of his word, it pleases him to exhibit him self unto us) do
remain and contynewe.

And is not this a new Gospel, to teach a Sacrament to be a God? to teach
that the bread (which is a vile creature) is very God, and that it ought to be
worshypped with all divine honor and worship? The sacrament that Christ made
and ordained to be a memorial of his death and redemption by him: to be made
Christ him self, is it not blasphemy? A piece of past which was made but
yesterday, can it be made a sacrifice to take away sin without blasphemy?
If a man should call the sacrament of baptism god, and do al godly honor
thereunto: would you not say he were mad? And yet is Baptism the chief
sacrament, both because it is the first sacrament (...) sign wherein the free
mercy of God is declared and opened unto us: and that in it no les, the^ in
the other, we do receive the promises of God, and his holy spirit, to the
confirmation of our faith and sure trust in him.

water, but I will baptize you in the name of the holy ghost. And for a plain
evidence and toke^ of the same he sent down the holy ghost in a visible
form, both upon the Apostles and them that they baptized in his name.

Thus you would blind us with your Sophistry, and make us to believe that it

accide^tes and no God. Moreover, if it chance you to touch it with your

and become passible otherwise: then is it only the form, the outward
accidents, the qualities, and dime^sio^s, and no God. But you deceive your
selves with vain words, and therefore, like as you do break the outward

The answer to Doctoure Damascen, whom Wynchester rehearses in greek.
FOr the testimony of Damascen) who^ you bring in as your chief wytnes) this
I have to say. First, he is a suspected person, being at the time when the
Pomp of the Romayne bishop or Antichriste, began to exalte him self above
every thing, that was god and godly.

Secondly, he maynteyned Idolatry with such contention, that he deserved to
have his right hand stryken of, and hanged in the markette place as an open
offender, ^oeth in that crime and other, whereof he was before the Emperor
Leo accused and condemned.

Thyrdelie, you would mayuteyne his honesty by the witness of an honest
man, Ecolampadius. But we discharge you of My Lord has lost his witness.
this testimony, euen-by the testimony of the same Ecolampadius, in the

Alberte, nor yet Dunsse, nor any of the new fellows: but Peter the patcher of
the se^tences: whom they call their master, who also has rubbed his error
upon other that patche up other men's wrytynges: As Damascen, and Gracian did.
Again a little after. Peradventure Damascen and other that followed him. write
in such sort, but the reader that is wise can be little moved thereby. For he
does by many arguments declare him self, neither to be sound nor
substantial. Again, Like as Paul said. When I was a child, I did speak
like a child: says he. When I had small knowledge, and had all things in
admiration, without judgment, I did write some things which now I do not
only not defend, but I wyshe them abolyshed and burned, if they be
unprofitably published in any place, and if I obtain my desire therein, I
will be glad and rejoice. By like this Ecola^padius repented the translatyng of
Damascen
book of Damascene (which he had translated) was one of them which he did not

Surely, Augustine, in that he made a book of retractations, willing us to
receive the wrytynges of no man farther then they are agreeable to the
scriptures: may teach us right well that we may refuse Damascene: I will
therefore ask none of your fellows: whether you be an honest man. But I will
try boeth Damascene and all your Doctors, by the infallible testimony of the
word of God. And because you do defend him with a miracle: we put you out of
doubt: such lyinge miracles, openly maynteynynge Idolatrie', cause us to
give the less credit unto him. For Christ says, that Antichriste shall
come with wonders and lyinge signs, in such sort, that the very elect (if
it were possible) shall be deceived. Wherefore, says Christ, if they say,
lo here is Christ, lo there is Christ, believe them not. etc.

The foundation whereupon our faith is grounded.
BUt I do take our doctors and read them with like judgment as I do the
Rabines of the Hebrews. That is to say, to be me^ learned and highly endued
with knowledge of secret things, and therefore that they ca^ open deaply hid
mysteries. But yet al men of judgment may know that they have their gifts but
unto a certain measure, and as they are me^, so do they err many times, in
the mattiers of most weight and importance. Whereby is wrought the marvelous
wisdom of God, who only will be accounted always true, vprighte and just in
all his words, and that all men should appear (as they are) liars. If in any
one man should rest the fulness of al truth, we would by our weakness very
proudely swear into his words, thereupo^ establish our belief, and make him
as it were an earthly God.

Paul therefore led by the spirit of God, takes his master Gamaliell and
the great Rabines, to no counsel in the setting forth of the high mysteries,
which God had reueiled unto him. No he would not confer with flesh and
blood, that is, with any man, notwithstanding he him self was wonderfully
enstructed in the law, and became irreprehensible therein, being a pharisei,
that is to say, an interpreter, and (as your men are) a doctoure him self.
Notwythstandynge he brings nothing of Thalmud, he teaches not hynge by the
traditious of their fathers, but by Moses, by the prophets, and the open
word of God, whereupon only faith can have his foundation. Faith is of
hearing says Paul, and this is by the hearing of the word of God, and not of
man's doctrine.

Though you therefore, do call this your doctrine of the real and carnal presence
of Christ under the form of bread and wine, the foundation of our faith: yet
were they never set in our old Creed and belief, nor nu^bred among the. xii.
articles of our faith. And Paul, when he said, I do only know Jesus Christ and
him crucified, which is the very foundation of our faith, whereby we might be
saved, though we lived in wilderness, or dyed upon the seas without this
sacrament. Yea though we be murdered in your presence and by your formentes put
to death, without the receyueinge of this Sacrament. For our ^ayth stands
fully grounded upon this word. Wh^ so ever confesses Christ to be come in
the flesh, he is borne of God, and who so ever believes and is baptized, the
same is saved. Add you hereunto what new foundations you please. We feel in
our hertes (being taught by the open word) that no man can No man can lay
any other foundation then Christ.
lay any other foundation but Jesus Christ. By whose death we dye from
confidence in all creatures, and by whose rysynge from death: we do rise again
and do seek things that are above, where Christ sits at the right hand
of God.

Of contrariety and co^tradiction.
THe Devil has an other piece of Sophistry, which is in conterfaite
Winchesters words.
contradictions, wherein he uses for a preface and introduction: a most
certain truth, which is, that truth agrees with it self, and has no
part contrary to an other. Wherefore, saying the word of God is an
infallible truth, it has no contrarieties in it self. All the world must
assent hereunto. But thus the Devil proceeds to his cauillations, from
things evidently true, by little change, to things evidently false. Heaven
and earth have a kind of contradiction, Christ is in heaven where saint
Stephane did se him. Ergo he is not in the earth, in the sacrament of the
aultare. Christ ascended into heaven, Ergo he taryeth not here. He sits at
the right hand of God, Ergo he is not in the sacrament of the aultare. He is
the creatoure. Omnia per ipsum sacta sunt. All things be made by him. Ergo, he
is not a creature made of bread.

He dwells not in the temples made with man's hands, Ergo he is not in the
box upon the high aultare.

Your solution to these open scriptures and The answre.
most evident arguments: is at one word, and that is this.

They be taken for notable co^tradictions Winchesters words.
and insoluble sophisines, and in effect, in all these arguments there is no
contrariety or contradiction in the things, but only a repugnaunce, and
impossibility to man's carnal capacity.

But I beseech you (good bishop) is there The answer.
no contrariety in the things? Is not heaven and earth clean contrary? Have
you so captiuated your wits, and dulled your understanding, that you ca^ not
perceive those two things to the contrary? God is the creatoure and maker of
all, therefore can he not be a creature made of bread. He dwells not in the
temples made with man's hands, for the heaven of heavens can not contain
him: therefore is he not enclosed in a little box, and hanged up by a band. It
is to much shame, for any priest, bishop, or christian man, to think so
irreverently of the secret majesty of God, as that he might be bound unto a
place, enclosed in a cake or a little box, saying boeth heaven and earth be
full of his dreadful majesty, and we, what so ever we be, do live, be moved,
and have our being of him.

He is infinite, incomprehensible, unmeasurable, higher then the high heavens,
lower then the deape and botomles waters, he measures the wide world with his
spanne, and co^teyneth all enclosed in his fiste. With him the light dwells,
and the sun beams are at his ordering. By him is ruled light and
darkedesse, life and death, and altogether. Wherefore when thou can^t enclose
in the box the rageyng seas, when thou can catch the move in a corner and
sparre her up in a case, when thou can pen up the sun (being but a
creature) in thy pix: then will I grant the to have power over things
infinite and incomprehensible. In the mean time I must take it impossible not
only by carnal capacity: but also by spiritual judgment grounded upon the
word of God, and by the gift of reason, whereby al men considering the work
of God in the cretion, may know their creatoure to exeell all creatures
far, and that he can therefore be made by no creature, neither of any
creature, much less can he be enclosed in a box of an y^che and an half
deape, when the priest will ^mble four words in a corner: and there lie tied
till he wax foystie, unless the priest lose him. Oh abominable Idolatours,
how much does this derogate to the majesty of God? And how far contrary
is this to his godly nature.

Now, that it is contrary to the human nature of Christ to be enclosed in
bread and sparred in a little box: thus mape we more largely prove unto you.

Christ in his human body, forsakes the world, he goes unto the father.
He did keep those that were his, so long as he was in the world. And when he
departed out of the world, he desired his father to keep them. He comforted
them when he went away, saying that it was profitable for the^ that he
departed, that the spirit of comfort might come. He promised to come again
visibly and with glory as he went, and in the scriptures there is none other
coming of Christ taught us, but the coming first in humilite to take our flesh
upon him, and afterward in glory, to judge all flesh, which things are
declared, Math. xxvi. Mark. xvi. Luke, xxiiii. John. xiii. xvi. xxii. Actuum.
i. vii. Romans viii. Ephe. i. ii. Corhi. vi. Hebru. viii. ix. x. xii. i. These.
iiii. i. Petre. ii. So that by the scriptures we must needs be compelled to
deny the body of Christ and his human nature, to be now any where upon the
earth, ^or else with the Marcionistes, must we take from him, the verity of
his body: and deny that he has a body according to our nature.

This thing does Augustine handle at large in the epistle he writes to
Dardamus, Augustine to Dardanius.
unto whom I send you that stick so much to doctors. There he teaches you,
that, as he is God, Christ is in every place. But in that he is man, he is in
heaven only, which all the scriptures do testify. And it is the chiefest
point of our belief, that he is in heaven and sits at the right hand of
the father.

Now our faith which can be grounded on no manne^ saying: can seek him in
non^ other place, but where the word of Christ declares him to be, saying
Christ him self warns us that false prophets shall come and say, lo here
is Christ, lo there is Christ, and commands us, that in nowife we believe
them. But we shall then only look for him when he shall come with such shine
and brightness, as is the lighteninge from the Math. xxiiii.
east to the west thorowout the whole world. Which words, though they may be
well understand of the fall and decay of al these outward rites wherein the
Jews and hypocrites of all times have set the high worship and kingdom of
God, and also of such seducers as would promise them selves false Christ's
and saviors: yet nevertheless as the spirit of God has al things present,
which are, which have been and shall be: so are the words of the spirit
general, serving for all times, fit, apt and meet to reprove al abuses. And
here may we plainly epsy that they are spoken against al manner of bodily
presence of Christ, both in the aultares here, and there in the bread, and in
the chambers and corners where he is holde^ up and showed between the priests
fingers to be worshipped.

But if you desire yet some one place of scripture so plain that it can not be
resisted, by any gloses or sophistry, but that it shall stand plain
contrary and cantradictorie to your doctrine, read the third of the Acts.
That heaven must receive and have Jesus Christ, unto the time that all things
be restored. Act. iii.
The words of that place are very plain, for he does not only make Jesus
Christ a very man, as Moses was, whose nature was not to be in two places at
once: but he adds also these plain words. That the heaven must receive
this same Jesus Christ unto the time that al things be restored. Que^ oportet
celum accipere vsque ad tempus restitutionis omnium.

Thus do we proceed therefore. Christ has (by his departing, his sittynge at
the right hand of his father, and returning again at the time appointed) so
plainly appointed by the scriptures, one only place where we shall seek his
natural body: that, so many of us as will not strive against the manifest
truth can not double, but that his body remains there only, where he
shows him self to be. We conclude therefore, that it is contrary to
Christ's religion to seek him upon the earth enclosed in a box.

Secondly, Christ has showed where he will be until the day of judgment,
that is to say, at the right hand of God his father, till that he has made
all his enemies his footstool. Wherefore we can seek him in none other place,
with sure fayeth to find him.

Thirdly against your whole doctrine, (that the body of Christ may be
infinitely scattered thorowout the world and your words a little after
following, which are that the human body is not diuisible by time or place,
wherein you do confound the natures of Christ (...) give that unto the ma^hode,
which is only the propriety of the godheade, and so open the way unto two
heresies) we have the plain testimony of the Angel. You do seek Christ
crutified, he is risen, he is not here. Where as if his ma^hode had been
infinite as is the godhead: the^ should he have been there present. For no man
ca^ deny but there was his godhead presently. Neither ca^ you escape by this
cauillatio^, that then he is infinite, indivisible (...) without
circu^scriptio^ of time or place when you will have him, like as you do multiply
your cakes into millions and thousa^des of thousa^des at Easter, which do al
perish as it were in a moment, for that which is infinite or indivisible
cannot chaung the nature to have his bonds and finite order aypoynted him,
Wherefore we do most truly call God and his power only infinite: where man in all
his nature has his determinate measure of substance, qua^tities, qualities and
knowledge, as appears in Christ (who as he was very man) did not know the
hour and time of the day of judgment of all flesh, was enclosed in the
grave, and did walk upon the earth and appear always unto his disciples in
that sort and manner, that at no time any occasion might be taken that he
infinitely did fill all places, no not that at any time he might appear to be
in two places at once, all his miracles do so faithfully witness and report the
truth of his human nature, and natural body, which your vain opinion of
enclosing him in bread, and making him infinite, goes about to subvert.

But now when you have no scripture to prove your mattier true, that Christ as
he is man, may be in heaven and yet fill all the Aultares of the earth: you do
run to the saying of Esaie the prophet. If you believe Esaie. vii.
not, you shall not understand. The which words being spoken to Achas and
the unfaithful house of David, that was afraied at the coming of two kings of

If you do not believe: the cause is, you will Obstinacy is the cause that you

not be faithful. And so agrees it well with the words following, when Achas

I marvel (bishop Stephane) that you wax not ashamed of your writing. You

that here is a wonderful miracle wrought, but you know not how it is

But in this sophistry, the devil makes man Winchesters words.

For soeth here you speak untruly of us. For we al do believe in heart and
confess with The answer.
mouth: that God only is almighty, and fills all the heaven and the earth

Where as you deride this thing, that every man should make a sermon: I
wyshe that every man could do it, and will exhort them that can do it (ene^
for the love of God) that they do it more diligently. For I do nothing fear

al our conforte, al our hope must be of the spirit. For what so ever is borne

lyffe, and to them only that have this spirit in their hertes, to the^ I say,

The complaint of God against Idolatours
Hear the word of the Lord thou proud Babylon. Thou people of Sodom and
spiritual Egypt: hear the word of the Lord? For asmoche as the lord Jesus
Christ, is daily crucified, daily slain, daily set forth in mocking sacrifice:
the blood of the testament is trode^ under foot and the arc of the covenant is
driven away. He that despises the law of Moses, says the Lord, is under.
ij. or. iij. witnesses condemned: and how much more shall he be punished,
that treads under fo^e the son of god, despises his word, and does
vnhalow the blood of the testament whereby he was sanctified, and works
co^tumeliously against the spirit of grace? It is God (O you princes of Sodom)
that gives sentence in this matter. Before the high Judge shall you be
condemned (you seed of Babylon) because it has pleased God to admonish you,
first by Moses and then by the prophets, and last of al by his own son to
turn into the way of truth. But you contrary wise, do wyllingly follow the
way of wickedness. And whereas the Lord sends daiely for the fruit of his
vini^^rd* you entreat his servants at your pleasure, Some of them you do beat
some other you slay, and that more is, you do neither reverence nor forbear
his only begotten son, but rageynge like men in a furye, you have with one
whole consent taken him, slain him, and cast him out of the vyneyarde, which
was his own enheritaunce.

Hear therefore the^ wicked nacio^, and know that he whom thou have cast
away: in the corner stone where upon whatso ever buylding is stablisshed, it
grows up to be a holy temple unto the Lord, and who so ever does fall upon
this stone, he shall be shaken in pieces which thing the Jews sto^blyng upon
his The ruin of the gentiles is at hand.
humiliti, do show unto the world to have* ben truly spoken, even like as the
ru^n^ of the gentyls shall shortly declare, upon whom (...) uer this stone
shall fall, for he shall most spedily be broken to powder that the whole world
may at le^gh learn, how horible a thing it is to fall into the hands of the
living God, whose vengaunce is sore and greuouse against his enemies, Like as
his mercy is ready toward the children of mercy, the Ninevites for an example,
who at the preachinge of Jonas only, did penance in ashes and sakclothe, and
so escaped the aduengeynge hand of the almighti. But you that live now in the
later end of the world, being admonishede by a thousand oracles and
warninges of the prophets, threateninge battle, famine an pestilence: do not
change your wicked purpose, but suffer all the words of Christ his prophets
and Apostles concerning the wrath of God in the later days: to be spoken in
vayn. No man, renueth his heart, no man changes his manners. There is not one
that Noman ame^deth his manners.
does good, no not one. But the more that your wyckednese is opened by the
scripturs the more that Moses chasteneth your malice: the more earnestly that

Judgment. Wherefore morn and houle Oh you wicked, upon the miseries which shall
chance unto you, you I say, which are the inue^ters of new Idols and the
dispisers of me your euerlasteing God. For your god (in whom your hope rests)

sparks of fire, and your selves into stubble, and your Idols shall be br^t.
there shall be none to quentche it, Once I will awake, and not always suffer so
great reproach as to be dispiced, where a dead Idol which has neither sense,
moueynge, life nor breath shall be received and embraced.

It is I (I say), that does give life and breath to al creatures, it is I
that lend stre^gh and all the natural powers, which you do mispe^d in making
of your Idols, utterly for getting that I am the same that made your parent
Adam unto mine own likeness, I adourned and decked him with no small gyfts
Reason and judgment I gave him, and ordained him governor over al other
creatures You have forgotten also, that immediately after this my great mercy

creator chose rather to be subject unto the most vile creature of al foloyng

God therefore, does unto this day dwell under my The new found god is

Again after that man kind was increased and wickedness did grow more and

But away with this gross blyndenesse (O you sophisters) for all men may
perceive that you love to walk in darkness. According to your gross and
carnal imaginations therefore, and after the dullness of your capacities
which can perceive no spiritual things, because you are not borne of the

talk in matteir that shall be open unto the commune senses and judgment of all
men, may cause you to harken to my voice, and perceive your own blyndenesse.

Oh how gross opinions have you conceived of me the Lord God? How leudly do
you esteem my power infinite, which do think it possible that I the living
God creatoure and maker of heaven and earth: should be changed, or would be
consecrated into bread, wine, stock, stone or any other creature. This is not
consecration or holy making: but this is contamination, polutinge and defilyng
of the name of God with intolerable blasphemies.

My sacrate majesty (to bring you out of doubt and error, O you miserable
men) can suffer no such alteration nor change, of God is not chaungeable
fourmes insensible. Wherefore, if ye require in me (the God incomprehensible)
the poetical chaunges of Jupiter: you are worse the^ mad. For I am (...)? I
am, I have been, and shall be. I am God evermore and not changed. What

years that does feel* none age. For a thousand years are but one day in my
syghte. For in the twynckelynge of an eye, do I behold all things, be they
present, paste, or to come.

Your Saturn whom you hang up in a cord as a wicked fellow: had need to

I appeal to your own conscience in this mattier, your conscience (I say)
that do make and mar so many Gods in so little space, you (I say) that do
seek out so strange ingines for the preservation of your Gods. The fear of
a mouse causes all this defense.
You close him in a box of harder metal then myse teeth can penetrate, you
hang him up in a cord lest the gredie myse should besiege him, you cover
him with a canopie, so that the myse can not come at him: and what means all
this, but that you know by experience, that the myse do nothing fear him,
because he is made but of bread, and has no life in him nor hardiness to
beat a mouse? Let your own conscience be Judge in this mattier.

But O wicked Idolatours. If this were God that you do this handle, he would

strength. How be it he can do nothing. Or if he can do any thing, cry upon
him as did the priests of the old Idolatours that he will do so much as put
one horn out of his shel and box wherein he is enclosed; to assray his enemies,
or else to your great confusion, he shall be less set by then a creping snaple.
Or if you dare make a proof of his power: leave him without but one night out
of his box, and you shall see the little mise will not be much afraid of him,
neither do the cattes, backs, owls, swallows, and sparowes greatly fear
him. Then tell me I pray you, why man should be so mad as to stand in fear
of the thing which is of no reputation.

Of the word sacrament,
ABout the word sacrament,. I inte^de not long to trifle. But to take your own
words and somthinge to examine them. You do bring in an argument of your
adversaries, made by the strong places of reasoning called. Definitiorei, in
english the definition of the thing, that is (to them that understand not these
terms) grounded upon the oracion or sentence that declares what the thing
is. The definicion of a sacrament.


A sacrament therefore, is (as well by the definition that your doctors have
made, as that you your self do make) a visible sign of an invisible grace.
Upon this definition follows a double argument. First, because it is a sign:
it is not the thing signed or tokened. And this reasone is proved true, a
relative. oppositis (if you have learned so much logike) and by many fold
examples. As the ale pole, the yuie bush, being the signs of wine and ale
within the tavern house: can not be the thing signed and tokened. your. (...)
for ked myter signifiynge the. ij. laws can not be. ij. laws. Your white
rachet signifiynge chastity: can not be chastity it self. Your glitteringe
shoese: signifiynge the preciouse fete of the preachers of the gospel: are not
the fete signed and tokened. Your broad shaven A broad shaue^ crown is the
sign of folishuesse.
crown signifiyng folishnesse: is not the thing it self, I trow unless you
have changed all the things into their signs and shadows You have caused us
long, and would have us still, to gape after signs and shadows as the dog
does in Isopes fables, and so lose the thing it self which should be our
fode and confort. You tell us, that the sign token or shadow: is the thing
it self. Shall we believe you still?

Nay, your definition tells us of two things to be in this sacrament. That
is to say, Two things are to be considered in asacrament.
A visible sign, and an invisible grace. What other thing (I pray you
without contencion) can this visible sign be, but the bread which Christ
takes in hand and breaks? For other visible thing there is* none.

That is to say in plain english (that all men may know what we speak and
write) there is none other things open to the eyes of man to be seen.

This bread thus broken therefore, is the sign or token (that may be seen) of
a grace, that can not be seen. That is to say of the forgiveness of sins in
this blood of the new testament of Christ our savior.

Thus frame I therefore the secounde reasone. A thing visible and invisible can
not be boeth one, to be senne and not seen. But One thing can not be boeth
visible and invisible
this sacrament (as you have confessed in your definicion) is a thing visible
and may be seen: therefore can it not be the thing invisible, thereby
represented. All that you have spoken in this cause (byshoup Stephane) is of
your own head, without either scripture or reasone.

But lo now the wily fox, stealeeth into agreate borough where he waloweth

But if a man keep him from takeynge air at this change: he wylbe smothered

call it bread again.

But because you can prove no change: Nothing like Exodus iiii.
your similitude of the rod of Moses (which was turned into a serpent and
strenght way returned to a rod again) is not like. For the same rod was
afterward declared (ever in the sight of Pharao and all the Egiptians) to be
the aduengeing rod of God whereby all the waters of Egypt were turned into
blood, and all the wonderful plages wroughte, which are terrible unto us,
unto this day. Worthily therefore, was this called a rod, for it was the
chastesyng rod of God, and always returned into a rod again, so often as
Moses or Aaron did take it in their hands.

Now for that you bring Jacob for your purpose, there was no change of
substance in him: for he was still Iacobbe, and his house was still called the
house of Jacob through out all the prophets, as well as Israel.

To this I answer, that the Romeish church had the scriptures, but the

of his doctors: and so be sinered with the black coals of their helly
doctrine, that their souls should never be clear again, as for all other pore
men, not brought up in the popeishe learning of his schools and therefore
haueing their consciences like a white wall, ready to receive all truth of God
his holy word: the scripture was clearlie forboden them, like as you have

To the bishops.
IT may well appear what minds you bishops have to the furtheraunce of the
knowledge of God: by that you do with out cause, find fault with the diligent
translations of good men, co^demnyng them by your counsayles, and yet will not
translate any part thereof your selves. Yea all your life and labors do teach
us plain, that you would stop our eyes and lead us capty^e in your blind
ways. Therefore if we should follow you being blind guides, false prophets
and Idol pastors: we shall be still scattered abroad in the blind ways of
ignorance, we shall be led with your lies even together with you into the
blind pit of darkness. Thus have you led our fathers before us, so many as
would take you for their scho masters, and had none other secret motion of
the spirit, to lift their hertes up into the heavens, d^nge the aid and
healpe of al other ^r^

And yet (...) can not content your selves with the kingdom that you have
usurped in the consciences of men (where none ought to reign but God) more
then these thousand years: unless you may still have the same authority in
establishinge your popetrie and Idolatry, beating evermore into our ears,
that your Idolatrous and superstitious religion, has continued these. M. D.
years. Where as we partly have declared, and might more at large declare (were
it not to tedious) that it has crept up only with your wicked papacy and
possessions of the church, and has continued only the time that Satan has
been lose and sent forth into the world to work his will, when you his stout
soldier did shit up the kingdom of God his word, and neither would enter
in your selves, nor suffer them that would enter. But now that the lamb has
unlocked the book: Satan begins to roar for fear of the fall of his
kingdom, and you bishops (his Satan begins to roar.
champions) do rage and fight against God his word, yea against every thing

the word of his witness. And therefore do we ieoperde our souls unto death,
not only against the Romish Antichriste: but the Mahumetaine also who is like
to reign over us as a worthy plage for slidynge from the word of God, eue^ as
he has many years reigned over many christian nations, which boeth in life
and learning were as holy as we be now co^pted.

If this thing (I say) shall come to pass (as no man knows Gods secret
working but such only as it shall please him to endue with this knowledge) we
shall be ready, both to speak and write, as we now do, for the glory of God,
against al Idolatours so far as God shall open our hertes and give us strength.
For without his audacitie and boldness of spirit poured into us: we shall
stand in as gerate fear to perform this, as we should be to write against
your abominations, knowing your cruelty toward the^ that have hertofore
moved your patience.

Give none ear to the words of these prophets that deceive you. For they

Thus are we plainly taught how perilouse a thing it is, to follow the
doctrines of men, be they never so highly advanced with titles of holiness.
Yea we are by the mouth of God admonished above all things to beware of them
that promise peace and quietness, folowinge but the shreudnesse of their own
hertes and folishe inventions, for it is a kind of Idolatry, not to stick
unto his word, as unto the thing only sufficient. Of such prophets
therefore, as bring their own inventions: does he say. I did not send
them, and they ran. I did not speak unto them, and they did prophecy. If
they had stand in my counsel and published my words to my people, they
should have turned them from their wicked ways, and from their wicked
inventions. I did hear how they told lies and dreams in my name by the
disceites of their heart, causynge the people to forget my name for their
dreams, (as is it come to pass this day) Therefore says the Lord of
hosts against such prophets. He that has a dream, let him tell his dream,
and he that has my word let him Ezechi. xxxiii
speak my word truly. What minglest thou chafe with the ^heate? Are not my

Therefore to you prophets, that steal my words, every one from his brother,
dreamynge forth your lies deceyuyng my people with your lies and your miracles,
where as I did never send you, nor yet command any such thing to my people
as did not profit them. You are the heavy burden that I can no longer bear
and therefore I will cast you away.

Woe unto the shepeherdes of Israel (says the Lord) which do feed them
selves, The true de scription of our prelates.
ought not the flock to be fed of the shepeherdes? But you have eaten the
milk, you are clothed with their woll, you sley that which is fat and feed
your selves and will not feed my flock. You conforte not the weak, you heal
not the sick, you bind not up the broken, you seek not that which
perishes, but with power and rigor do you rule over them. Thus are my sheep
scattered because they have no shepeherde, and devoured with wild beasts.
They go wandering in the mountains and are scattered through the earth, and
no man does seek them. No man does seek them, I say. As truly as I do live
(says the Lord God) because my flock is thus spoiled and my sheep denoured,
whylse the shepeherdes do feed them selves and despise my flock. Lo, I my
self will require my flock at the hands of these shepeherdes, and they shall
neither feed my flock nor yet them selves any longer. For I will deliver my
flock out of their mouths says the Lord.

This is the talk that God the father has thorowout the old testament
against you that will not be content to feed his flock with his word only,
without the sour leven of man's doctrine. He calls you men fed and led with
the wind of errors, Idol shepeherdes, yea devouring wolfes that will never be
saciate.

Saying then, that boeth the scriptures and your own lives do testify of you,
that you are such rotten trees or rather poisoned stocks: what fruits of
heavenly doctrine shall we look to spring from you? Do men gather grapes of
thorns, or figs of thystles? The yuyl tree ca^bring no good fruit. Christ
therefore (in the new testament, and in his first sermon) gives us warnyng
of such Idol shepeherdes, saying. Beware of Math. vii.
these false prophets which come to you in shepes clothing, for inwardly
they are rauenyng wolfes.

And after that he had rebuked them that Math. xvi.
would seem to know al things, and yet could not see the time of their

teach the traditous of me^ to put the precepts of God out of place, and that

fathers. Math. vi. Math. xxiii.
For couetise, worldly pomp and hypocrisy: do establishe all the works and

Read the damnation that Christ him self pronounces against you in the.

far Mat. v.
pass the ryghtuousnes of the scribes and phariseis (who only were accounted
