The state of the phariseis and you (O bishops, lest you should murmour and
grudge The phariseis and bishops al one.
at my plain wrytynges) is in this case of your doctrines for the feeding of
Christ's ^locke, all one. Neither has any of you authority either to make
laws or interpret the scriptures (for boeth have one strength and must be
done by the same spirit) you have none authority, I say, over the flock,
further then you have the word of God for you. And bringing that word, you
may say: he that despises you, despises God.

As for things indifferent, you must say as Paul said upon this your own
exe^ple. If any man be co^tentiouse: the church of God knows no such
custom. So that rather then any such bitter contention as is now adays,
should continue it were better that all your in uentions were refused. For
saying that your authority is given to edify by love and charity: you may
not abuse it and destrye by bitter braulynge and cruel contention, for such
things as were not good before you named them so, nor yuyl before you did
forbid them.

Thus do I take many of your doctrines of men to be indifferent. As to stand
up at the Gospel, to pray or preach bare headed, to eat fish this day or
that day. All these things being indifferent in their kind, that
Superstition makes all things evil
is to say, nothing yuyll being voyed of superstition: are by superstition
made yuyll. For that changes good into yuyll. Yet are the best of these
doctrines but vain worship John. iiii.
of God, even in their best use. For his worship stands in spirit and truth.

But you have other doctrines and that very many, that are manifestly yuyll,
because you do therein adulterate the word of God as did the phariseis when
they added their gloses to the commandments of God. As when God said. Thou
shalt love thy neighbor: they added, hate thine enemy. God said. Thou
shalt not swear, but they added unto the precepte. Pay unto the Lord the
thing that thou swearest. Again, did not the old pharisees with their sour
leue^, Math. vi.
(which is Hypocrisy) make vnpleasante and unsavory the two special works
of the new man, Fasting and prayer. Did not Christ him self continually
rebuke them, Math. xv.
because they brake the commandments of God for their own traditions and
doctrines? where God the father had given commaunmente to honor father and
mother: they cried for their gain, their corban and offerynges.

Where God asks the whole heart and thereof only measures all our doings:
their teaching is to worship with the lips, though the heart be far from
me, says the Lord by his Prophet. In vain therefore do they worship,
teaching the Esai. xxix.
doctrines as precepts of men. The which doctrines, sith their first
beby^^ynge, the true Prophets of Christ seekynge the only honor of God:
have from time to time, labored to confute, and to restore to their worthi^es,
the precepts of God, and his holy commandments which ever more (amongst
hypocrites) have been in small reputation in comparison of their own
inventions. In so much that all these Prophets whom God sent to beat down the
blind errors of men's dreams: were hated, persecuted from City to City,
scourged, slain and crucified. So that all the blood of the just which was
and shall be shed upon the earth from Abell to the worlds end: may be heaped
upon the Hypocrites in the day of aduengeaunce, when they shall be adjudged to
the fire and torments prepared for the Devil and his Angels.

If any man do not fully perceive by this we have spoken, that the old
Phariseis and ours be not all one in their doctrines, their Hypocrisy and
cruel tiraunie: I desire him to considre the mattier depely, and to compare
substantially, the old and new things together. Concerning the holy words
of our Math. v.
master Christ, and most deep opening of the law of God his father, corrupted
by the gloses of the old Phariseis: our new Phariseis have found out a new
doctrine. They say that Christ's words are counsayles and no precepts. And
thereof have they founded and grounded opera supererogationis. Works that they
may distribute for money. For fasting Math. vi.
and praying (which are the new wynes that will break the old vessels) he
that has eyes may see that the old phariseis were not so yuyll as are the
new, who have added more to the wickedness of their predicessours. For where
Christ did rebuke the other bu^ of hypocrisy and vain glory. Ours have
added herunto, superstition of days, times, meats and drynkes, and have made
their prayers utterly nothing but a lip labor, because it is done in
appointed words and prescript number, in a tongue that the man which prays
does not understand. And therefore his lips labor, but his heart is voyed
of knowledge what he says, wherefore it can have no profit.

The honoring of the father and mother: they count chief^y to be done in their
corban, Math. xv.
offering mass pence and trentalles for them when they be dead. Much worsse
is this point then that of the old Phariseis.

To turn away the heart from the living God, that delivered out of Egypt:
They Math. xxiii.
have sought up and maintained ten thousand Idols. They bind heavy burdens of

Beware of such false prophets (says our Math. vi.
master Christ) they come unto you in shepes clothinge, but inwardly they are

If the black Morian may change his The morian and leopard^

Your doctrine stands only in meat and drink, which is nothing of the

not the wine, for then thou will judge it to tarry still unchanged in his

Fish you say is an holy meat in this your superstition. Thus hurt you the
body, and by your bodily doing, do nothing further true holiness. For God him
self is a spirit, and is worshipped in spirit, not in carnal doctrine and

Therefore (says Paul) if you be dead with Christ from traditions of the
world: why are ye (as yet living in the world) led with their Colo^^. ii.

Mark how Paul calls all your doctrines (...) will holiness. Because Will
holiness
they come of your fond wills, and of no precept or commandment of God.
Such is your doctrine forbidding men to receive the sacrament in boeth the
kinds (make the best you can of it) grounded (...) will holiness. For you say
that the sacrament is not ministered in both the kinds as Christ did distribute
it: because we lay men will not have it. If we lay men have any such will
contcarie to the will of Christ (who said, Bibite ex hoc omnes, drink of
this you all. Diuidite inter vos, divide this among you) it is a fond will
holiness, and chosen holiness. But you say we do forbear it of a reverence.

If it be good to follow our will holiness and fantastical reverence in this
kind: why do we not of like reverence forbear the bread also, lest it wax
clammy and cleave to the roufe of our mouths? for in the wine we feel ^one
so vnreuerent a thing. But for spillynge the wine your doctrine is that we
may not meddle there with. But we think there is far more danger in your
great sleaues and Faunelles when you turn, toss and toye over and about the
cup: then in us that have the cup holden to our heads like babes. So that
if it be well done upon such reverence to forbear the wine: you (upon whom
much greater danger hangs) ought to have the greater reverence. Therefore
are either you vnreuere^t, or else are we not reverent, but folishe in our will
holiness, so many of us as will not drink of this cup as our master Christ
has commanded us.

This is like the reverence that the kentishmen had to the kings horse when
the The kentishe man.
king commanded him to open the gate. Iche am not worthy (quod he) to open
the gate to my master your horse, but hereby dwells master Pecham a man
worthy to do it. In like manner do they that will not come to drink of the cup
of the new testament, when Christ commands them, saying with the kentishe
man. Iche am not worthy to toutch it nor to drink there of: but our master
person or our sir John are worthy men for the purpose.

But (oh blind bishops) we are not all so fond, to be illuded still. For
many have read your books written for this purpose to maynteyne your pomp and
to keep us as your underlings: and therefore will we no longer suffer you to
say that we lewd men will not have it. But we desire and require you for the
love of God in his son Christ by whom we are made al one perfect and knigeli
priesthod to offer up our selves a lyueing sacrifice, purified by the blood of
his unspotted lamb, which makes perfect all things in this uewe testament,
which he commands us to divide and generalli wills us all to be partakers
thereof, that you do set up no doctrine of will holiness against the manifest
word of Christ the son of God who said. Drink of this you all. For if you
do, it must neades be still spoken of you that is said by the prophet Esaie.
They worship me in vain, teachinge the doctrynes and precepts of men.

Now lest any simple man should be deceived Beware of my Lords lies.
with your iuglinge words, when you say that good men might by the order of

The communion under boeth kinds is not (...) unto lay men unto salvation.

And it is rightly and justly in old time decreed by the church: that they

Which they prove by these worthy reasones. For the^ were it dainger lest the

Christ was not ware in commaundeynge the wine to be taken: I do answer, that
Christ did forse the thing, but he kept it secret to prove the wisdom of his
church.

There is also an other inconvenience, For the body of the Lord must be kept
in Cibario, to be given to the sick. But if the wine should be reserved also:
it would be made vinacre, and so for the corruption, it should be no longer
blood. Ye^ the lutherians would deride us sayeinge, does it not well appear
that there is wine still. And so this should make against the opinion of
traunsubstantion and change of substance.

Thyrdely, this is also reasonable, that the priests should have some
privilege, to suppress and hold down the pride of the people.

Fourthly, this does auayll to prove the opinion. De concomitantia, of what so
ever the Lutherians do clatter, that we should follow, observe and keep, the
ordinances of Christ which he has appointed for our infirmity.

Also there should be an other daynger if the blood should be given to drink,
for the^ the taste thereof might engender a suspicion to the lay men there
remained wine still, whereof would arise many slanders.

But if they do reason that the church has no power to dispense with the

Let us go farther with your farthinges therefore. What makes a bishop? An

But Paul sets forth other manner of farthinges, where he describes a
bishop. The bishop (says he) must be fautles, the husband of one wife,
watchful, sobre, mild harberouse, apt to teach, no drunckarde, no fighter,
not desirouse of filthy gain, but vprighte, flyinge strife, flyinge
covetousness, that rules his own house well, which has his children in
subjection with al reverence. Lo, here be farthinges of great weight and value,
even when they be considered every one alone by him self. These are the good
farthynges therefore, that make the good bishops, and the other are the
nothinges that make the Idol bishops, things of no value. All the first
farthinges may well be wyped away and the man never the worsse: but wype
away these farthynges that Paul names, and you can have no good bishop.

Now for the substance of our religion which as you say stands in these

But learn, O bishop, I pray you, that all your nothings are not regarded

Thus by degrees come you to the high mystery of wickedness. And this causes
you that you can not be contented with the state of bishops, but you will be
Lords, yea above lords and princes, as you do both preach and write, because

substance of your religion. And therefore do you now fight with fire and
faggot, for the conservation of the same, that it may conserve you in your
lordly dignities.

Thus has your worldly witted fathers even from the beginning fought with the
saints of God, whose blood cries from under the aultare and asks
vengeance, and shall be heard right spedily.

worthily burned with fire, and (as you did rashly determine and judge)
condemned and destroyed in body and soul?

What were they? whoremongers, Idolatours, adulterers, thieves, extorsiouers, or
ma^quellers? Upon such comes the wrath of God, and such have no part in the
kingdom of God. But you suffer to live and you show no power against them. No
you are not any thing terrible unto such: for they dwell at your noses, they
eat at your tables, and are The bishops darlinges.
your darlinges. But who that speaks any thing against your popish Idols
and brainsicke inventions (have he never so faithful an heart to God, and be he
never so trusty to his prince) yet must he be an heretic, a traitor a lowlar
and all together.

This does the world epsy at the length and talks of you. I would this
talk might make you leave your evil doings: and to learn at the least to
do some part of your duty before the wrath of God fall upon you. But I do
fear me al words are but wind with you. Only vexation and chastisement will
give you understanding. For lo, here you say full finely and like a popish
prelate that would have all thing brought to the old blyndenes and
ignorance, and to such captivity, and bondage that no man should talk of
his fayeth but under my Lords license, though Peter commanded the contrary.
You say that of faith there is so much talk and tattelinge (to use your own
terms) that true belief is gone. Surely if you call this true belief, the
Romish belief of pardones and pilgrimages, when we might have no talk of
^ure faith, but were commanded in pain of cursinge, and burninge, to beleue^
as the church of Rome believes, like as you can know none other true church,
nor none other good men, but such as follow that church: I grant your belief
is fore wasted, and I trust shall right shortly consume like stubble with the
fire of Gods word, and true works of mercy, peace, and loving kindne^
shall spring forth when men (knowing tha^ your Pope holy works are but the
madness of idle brains) shall worship the living God in spirit and truth. But
lo, you will have here the carte to go before the horse, and will have us to do
these works before we know them, saying that doing is the way to knowledge,
where contrary wise, al well doing must needs spring of knowledge, as the
only thing that makes our deeds good.

And because you bishops are so slow in preaching good works that God
requires: the people must needs be stacke in doing them. For you should be
the salt of the earth. The salt is ^^sauourie.
But saying that you be become unsavory, how ca^ you season other? You
preach your own inventions, the precepts and commandments of men, and them
must we needs know and confess, or else must we be brent. But it is a
dangerous thing to know the scriptures (and especially for pore men) and to
talk of our fayeth. This doctrine of yours spoyleth us of fayeth, and
brings us into the Idleness of works. Oh diuelishe sophistry, and the
spiritual subtlety, stryuing against all godliness.

Satan him self could not divise such a reason to hinder our faith and stop
knowledge. The Popes bishops only could do it.

But mark how this sophistry is confirmed and proved. The Bishop (for
lack of scriptures) brings forth Cato an heathen man who despised the greek
poets, because the youth of Rome waxed effeminate, and whi^se Cato.
they set their delight in them, they rather rejoiced in readinge of battayles
then fightinge them selves. But what is this to us christen men, which ought
to be ready to give answer of our faith to e^e^ie one that asks us? which
should talk of the will of God toward us, and his holy commandments when
we lie down and when we rise, when we go by the way and when we sit at the
table, compting our selves then to be most happy when we were most delited
therein, day and night as David says.

But this is strange doctrine unto you, because you are none of Paul's
bishops. For he gave his bishops in commandment to be iustant in the word in
time and out of time. No, you are an english bishop, thynkinge the word of
God to be good but at An English bishop.
those times that you will appoint, and that to a few gentlemen to whom you
durst not deny it. And to busily occupied merchants whom you do epsy not
so much to regard it as they have done, giuinge them this knot in the end of
your book, that (...) they wax wa^ ton, they shall be put to silence as well as
women, and yomen are all ready.

Oh Stephane, this is thy work, as the chiefest english captitaine that ever
Antichrist had. For thou workest thy works as his enemy, but thou art his
friend. Thou wouldeste seem an Angel, but thou art a fiende.

I beseech all good men therefore, that as they tender their souls health,
they will take heed to your sweet poison and flattering words, and also to
your dark terms which you do bring forth of other languages. For by them
chiefly have we ben deceived, and ever sith we have mistrusted your fair
words, and marked the mattier in our own mother tongue and natural language.
We have by little and little, ever more and more espied your subtilties.

Before we had the Creed in English: we ^lde not know that this presence of
the body naturally and really, that is to say, in his very nature as he was
man and a sensible thing and substance, was contrary to three of the most
manifest article of our faith.

Moreover, where you add as a couclusion, fully proved and persuaded unto al
good men, that Christ is really present in the Sacrament (...) the aultare, to
feed our weak bodies and souls, whereby to make us strong to come to him
and ly^e without end: surely I can not perceive how you can persuade this
thing to any good man, that marketh the Articles of his fayeth concerning the
ascendyng of Christ, and his sittynge at the right hand of his father and
his coming thence to judge the quick and the dead, though you have with your
dark terms deluded and blinded many good simple souls, who^ you would not
suffer to have and know their belief otherwise then in the lati^e tongue, and
so taken at your hands, that you might mixed therewith your gloses, so craftily
handled and blinded with your sophistry terms (as really to be in the
sacrament which you say before is accidents) that the thing it self and
substance may be really in accidents. And then shall it not only be a
spiritual meat to feed the soul: but also a bodily fode to feed your
bodies like fleshly Ca parnaites that will eat Christ as he was man walkyng
upon earth, to the fode of your bodies.

To make you strong (you say) to come unto him. What strength is it whereby
you Fill the bealie to come to Christ.
come to him? Bodily, or spiritual? Oh men voyed of the spirit. You will feed
the body, to have the strength of the spirit to come un to Christ. Where
learned you any like lesson in the scriptures?

This is your well doing and well speaking without knowledge. First labor
for knowledge of the word of God and leave the subtlety of your own brain,
and you shall boeth speak more wisely and work more godly I warrant you.

Christ teaches in the. vi. of John, that to come unto him is to believe in
him, saying. He that comes unto me shall not be hungry, and he that believes
in me, shall never be thirsty. And a little after, he calls this the eatinge
of the bread of life, the eatinge of him self, and his flesh, saying. I am
the living bread that came down from heaven, if any man eat of this bread,
he shall love for ever. And the bread which I shall give is my flesh, which
I shall give for the life of the world. He that eats my flesh and drinks
my blood, has everlasting life. And he that eats my flesh and drinks my
blood, abides in me and I in him. Then answers he to the blind
Caparnaites, that would eat him really and bodily, as the meat of their
bodies. My words are spirit and life, the flesh profits nothing.
Wherefore I said unto you, that no man can come unto me, except it be given
him of my father. And this power given of the father to receive Christ: is
taught in the first of John. He came into his own (says John) and his own
did not receive him. But so many as did receive him, he granted them to be
made the children of God. They (think you) that did receive him bodily, and
eat him really (to use your terms) to feed their bodies and souls, to make
them strong to come to him.

What need such me^ to make the^ strong to come to him, when they have him in
their bealies, and have eaten him already?

Leave of all gross imaginations of the flesh that profits not, and follow
the doctrine of the spirit: and John will teach you and declare playnelie who
receives Christ and comes unto him. For all must needs be one thing, to
come to Christ and to receive Christ. Read this that ^oloweth therefore,
which you mumble up at every Mass in every corner, and yet will you not
suffer the people to understand it. Quotquot autem receperunt eum, dedit eis
vt liceret filios dei fieri, videlicet hijs qui credidissent in nomen ip^ius.
Quino^ exsanguinibus, neque ex voluntate carnis, neque ex voluntate viri, sed
ex deo nati sunt. So many as receive him, he granted the^ to be made the
children of God (that is to say) so many as believe in his name. Mark home
diligently John declares him self of the receiuinge of Christ by faith And
further Which are not borne of blood, neither by the will of the flesh, nor by
the will of man, but are borne of God, as 1. Pet. i.
Peter says. Borne again, not of mortal seed, but by the word of the
lyuinge God. i. Pet. ii.


This is the milk not of the body (says Peter) but it is the meat and
milk of the soul, that knows no gile.

Thus renneth all the scripture, by metaphors and borrowed speech from bodily
meat to spiritual meat, from the bodily teeth and eatinge, to the
spiritual eatinge by the soul, which can be done by faith only. So that he
which is not borne from above of the spirit: can neither see the kingdom of
God, nor come unto Christ, let him eat the bread (wherein you say is really
the flesh) so long as you lust. For this must needs be true. That which
is borne of the flesh, is flesh, and that which is borne of the spirit, is
spirit.

Even like as Moses set up the serpent in the wilderness, that so many as
would come unto it might be saved from the fiery serpents: so likewise was
the son of man exalted that all that do believe in him should not perish, but
have everlasting life.

Again. So has God loved the world, that he has given his only son, that
who so believes in him, shall not perish, but have life everlasting.

Again. He that believes in him shall not be condemned. And he that believes
not in him is condemned all ready, because he believed not in the name of the
only begotten son of God.

Thus may we see that faith (and not ea^inge of Christ really in the sacrament)
does ^aue, and bring life everlasting. And not to ^eleue in the only
begotten son of God: is ^amnation of body and soul. So is it not to ^enie
your gloses really present, and bodily ^aten. Yea mainteininge this gross
opinion: ^ou can not esteem him to be the son of the ^uinge God, nor believe
the work that his ^ather has wronght in his death.

For God the father did not send his ^ne in the form of bread or any other
creature, but only in the form of man, to the intent to exalt man thereby, to
make man of his householde, to give life unto man by his son Christ, to
raise him again with Christ and cause him to sit together with Ephe. ii.
Christ among the heavenly spirits. And to show forth in the world to come,
the passing richesse of his grace, in his godnesse toward us by Christ Jesus.

We believe in the only begotten son, which was made man to save the world*
wherefore we can not be condemned, though we do seek none other strange
belief of really present and bodisie eaten to feed the bodies, which things
are not taught in the scriptures.

You do not believe in the only begotten son made man, but made bread to
take away sins: wherefore unless you do repent, your da^natio^ is at hand,
because you believe not in the name of the only begotten son of God, which
is the only begotten son, as he is man, conceived by the holy ghost and
borne of the virgin Mary, not as he is bread blown with your stinkinge
breathes. Neither is he the only begotten son of God, as he is wine
whispered into your chalice.

How do you believe in this name (the only begotten son of God) when the
scripture teaches you that there is none other name under heaven, whereby men
should be saved, and yon do say that there is an other thing (which some
name the Mass, and some the sacrament of the aultare) that saves from sins,
and is a sacrifice boeth for the quick and the dead, and (as your man
Damascen writes) it purges all diseases and incommodities.

Furthermore. We do believe, that Jesus Christ is the Christ that is the
anointed of God to offer the sacrifice wherewyth only, the father could be
pleased, and therefore are we borne of God.

You do say, that you are the Christ's and anointed priests to offer still for
the sins of the people. Who is your father but he that would darken the
sacrifice of the only begotten son of God and sit in the temple of God,
boasting him self for God, being in deed the adversary and is lifted up
against every thing that is God or godly, the wicked man, the cursed child.

Again. God the father said, this is my dearly besoued son, in who^ I am
pleased and pacified, hear you him.

We believe this word, and will seek no further, but to this only begotten
and dearly beloved son of God. Neither to pacify the wrath of God for our
trespasses: nor yet to seek any other teacher of his will, then the son of
God, whom we are commanded to hear.

You will set up the Mass your own work to pacify the father for the
sins of the quick and the dead. You will have your own doctors to descant
new gloses, and these must the pore flock of Christ hear, believe and
confess, or else they shall be brent.

But to hear Christ, the only begotten son of god, speak in the
scriptures: is poison to al men under the degree of gentlemen, and punishable
by your laws, as in the cases of heresy.

What call you this, but to make the only begotten son of God an heretic?
Call you this the beleuynge in his name? Thus may we prove that you believe in
the Popes name, whose laws and wrytynges are reserved of certeyue men for
certeyue purposes and are as much practiced and more stoutely defended then
any thing that Christ commands.

Yea, how can we think but that you believe more in the Pope, when you defend
his Acts more styfly, then the laws of the living God?

What if it should be proclaimed, that no manner book concerning any part of
the Popes re^igion, should be brought into the Realm? and that al those
which are brought in already, should be brent, could you byshopnes bear
this thing so guietly as you did diligently labor to have all s^che books of
christen religion brent and banished?

But to make an end where we began. John says that every spirit that
contelleth Christ to be comen in the flesh: is borne of God. This do we
con^esse that deny him to be come in bread: wherefore we be borne of God. And
thus bele^ing in the (...) often son of God, we can not be condemned.

But that spirit which does not confess Christ to be comen in the flesh,
is not of. God. And this is the spirit of Antichriste of whom you have heard
that he shall come, and he is in the world already.

Now saying that we (so many of us as confess Christ to be come in the
flesh) be borne of God: why should nor we for the glory of our heavenly
father and for our salvation, be so ready to lay down our souls, in the
faithful hands of his c^todie, as the spirit of Antichriste, and the
children of this world are to speak and (...) ^or the mainteinaunce of Ido
atric, ^he kingdom of Antichrist, to their own (...) ^amnation. Worldly Pomp
and dignity, the maintenance of Idolatry and Popetrie: has caused the
bishop to write his book, and to rail against the truth. And shall not the
crown of glory (which can never decay, the glory of the only everlasting
God) steare faithful men to make answer for the truth against falsehode?
specially, saying that we have this plain testimony, spoken by the mouth of
our savior. He that confesses me before men him will I confess before my
father that is in heaven, and him that denies me before men, shall I deny
also, before my father and his holy angels.

If I be blamed, if I be imprisoned, yea if I be burned for Christ's cause and
the truth: yet am I happy, by the open testimony of Christ in Math. My name
shall be restored in the Math. v.
heavens in the book of life, to be a fayethfull witness. I shall be set at
liberty for ever with Christ the son of God, my body brent into ashes
(where it has put of mortality) shall be restored unto me much better,
immortal and incorruptible. If I lose wife and child, father and mother: I
shall receive for them an hundredth fold. And for advantage above all, for f^ll
recompense: life everlasting. Who will not be ammate and encouraged by such
large promises?

God save King Edward from all errors. God defend his tender age from all
^he subtle malice of al Hypocrites and tray^urs. The living God establishe his
heart in the way of the truth for ever and ever. So be it.
